# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes CNI Network Plugin Interface Architecture

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the CNI (Container Network Interface) integration: the CNI plugin invocation, the network namespace setup, the IP address management (IPAM) call, and the network plugin manager that coordinates CNI calls during pod creation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Search the kubernetes/kubernetes repository for all Go source files that implement the CNI (Container Network Interface) integration. Specifically, find:

1. Files that contain CNI plugin invocation code (e.g., executing CNI plugins)
2. Files that handle network namespace setup for pods
3. Files that contain IPAM (IP Address Management) calls or integration
4. Files that implement the network plugin manager that coordinates CNI calls during pod creation

Look for keywords like: cni, SetupNetwork, TeardownNetwork, namespace, ipam, network plugin manager, cni exec, cni call, pod sandbox, network setup.

Use a combination of searches:
- Search for "cni" in Go files in pkg/kubelet and staging directories
- Look for CRI shim implementations that handle networking
- Find network plugin implementations and managers
- Identify IPAM-related code

Return a list of all relevant files with their full paths.

Perfect! I have successfully created a comprehensive `answer.json` file documenting all Go source files implementing CNI (Container Network Interface) integration in kubernetes/kubernetes.

## Summary

The analysis covers **27 key Go source files** organized into the following components:

### **CNI Plugin Invocation**
- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go` - Primary entry point calling `createPodSandbox()` → `RunPodSandbox()` CRI call that delegates to container runtime to invoke CNI plugins

### **Network Namespace Setup**
- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go` - `NetworkNamespaceForPod()` function for namespace configuration
- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go` / `_windows.go` - Platform-specific namespace handling

### **IP Address Management (IPAM)**
- `pkg/controller/nodeipam/node_ipam_controller.go` - Node IPAM Controller managing CIDR allocation
- `pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidr_allocator.go` - CIDR allocator interface for IP assignment

### **Network Plugin Manager**
- `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go` - `SetupPodNetwork()` / `TeardownPodNetwork()` orchestration
- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go` - Runtime manager coordinating pod lifecycle
- `pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go` - Pod worker entry point

The execution chain flows from pod workers → kubelet network setup → kuberuntime manager → sandbox creation → CRI RunPodSandbox call → container runtime → CNI plugins, with IPAM controller pre-allocating CIDR ranges.

kubernetes/kubernetes repository:\\n\\n## CNI Plugin Invocation\\n\\nThe primary entry point for CNI execution is in **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go**, specifically the `createPodSandbox()` function (line 38). This function creates a PodSandboxConfig and calls `m.runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()` (line 68). This CRI gRPC call is delegated to the container runtime (containerd/CRI-O), which then invokes the appropriate CNI plugins based on the network configuration.\\n\\nThe pod sandbox configuration includes critical networking information set up by `generatePodSandboxConfig()` which includes DNS settings and references to the network namespace.\\n\\n## Network Namespace Setup\\n\\nNetwork namespace configuration for pods is handled in **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go** through the `NetworkNamespaceForPod()` function. This function is called during sandbox config generation to properly set up the network namespace path that will be used by CNI plugins to configure pod networking.\\n\\nLinux-specific namespace handling is in **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go**, while Windows support is in **pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_windows.go**.\\n\\n## Network Setup Orchestration\\n\\nThe overall network setup orchestration happens at multiple levels:\\n\\n1. **Pod Worker Level** (pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go): The pod worker's `SyncPod()` function coordinates the overall pod lifecycle\\n2. **Kubelet Network Level** (pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go): Contains `SetupPodNetwork()` and `TeardownPodNetwork()` functions that manage pod network setup/teardown\\n3. **Runtime Manager Level** (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go): The `SyncPod()` function orchestrates pod synchronization including sandbox creation\\n\\n## IP Address Management (IPAM)\\n\\nIPAM is handled by the Node IPAM Controller in **pkg/controller/nodeipam/node_ipam_controller.go**. This controller manages pod CIDR allocation on nodes. The actual CIDR allocation is performed through the `CIDRAllocator` interface defined in **pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidr_allocator.go**.\\n\\nThe IPAM controller allocates IP address ranges that are then used by CNI plugins to assign individual IPs to pods. The controller's `Run()` method continuously manages CIDR allocation for nodes in the cluster.\\n\\n## Sync Actions and Network State\\n\\nNetwork setup and teardown are tracked as sync actions in **pkg/kubelet/container/sync_result.go**, with constants `SetupNetwork` and `TeardownNetwork` indicating network operations during pod synchronization.\\n\\nNetwork readiness is tracked through the `NetworkReady` runtime condition in **pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go**, which indicates whether the container runtime's network is ready to accept pods.\\n\\n## DNS Configuration\\n\\nDNS configuration for pods is handled separately in **pkg/kubelet/network/dns/dns.go** (cross-platform), **pkg/kubelet/network/dns/dns_windows.go** (Windows), and is also part of the sandbox config generation.\\n\\n## Monitoring and Metrics\\n\\nThe startup latency of the first network pod is tracked in **pkg/kubelet/metrics/metrics.go** through `FirstNetworkPodStartSLIDuration` metric, helping identify CNI plugin performance issues. Pod startup latency tracking is implemented in **pkg/kubelet/util/pod_startup_latency_tracker.go**.\\n\\n## Summary of CNI Integration Flow\\n\\n1. Pod worker calls Kubelet's SetupPodNetwork()\\n2. Kubelet delegates to KubeRuntime manager's SyncPod()\\n3. createPodSandbox() generates PodSandboxConfig with network namespace via generatePodSandboxConfig()\\n4. NetworkNamespaceForPod() sets up the network namespace path\\n5. RunPodSandbox() CRI call is made to container runtime\\n6. Container runtime (containerd/CRI-O) invokes CNI plugins\\n7. IPAM controller has previously allocated CIDR ranges for the node\\n8. CNI plugins use allocated CIDR ranges to assign IPs to pod interfaces\\n9. Network setup is tracked through sync actions (SetupNetwork/TeardownNetwork)\\n10. Network readiness is checked before allowing pod execution\"\n}\n",
